scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.santa-ana.org">santa-ana.org</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Santa Ana</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span> <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">Saint Anne</a>") is the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> and second most populous city in <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimated its 2011 population at 329,427, making Santa Ana the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">57th most-populous city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.\n</p><p>Santa Ana is located in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>, adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_River" title="Santa Ana River">Santa Ana River</a>, about 10 miles (16&#160;km) away from the California coast. Founded in 1869, the city is part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">Greater Los Angeles Area</a>, the second largest metropolitan area in the United States with almost 18 million residents in 2010. Santa Ana is a very densely populated city, ranking <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population_density" title="List of United States cities by population density">fourth nationally</a> in that regard among cities of over 300,000 residents (trailing only <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>). In 2011 <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> ranked Santa Ana the fourth-safest city of over 250,000 residents in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Santa Ana lends its name to the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Freeway" title="Santa Ana Freeway">Santa Ana Freeway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Interstate_5_in_California" title="Interstate 5 in California">I-5</a>), which runs through the city. It also shares its name with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Mountains" title="Santa Ana Mountains">Santa Ana Mountains</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_winds" title="Santa Ana winds">Santa Ana winds</a>, which have historically fueled seasonal <a href="/wiki/Wildfires" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildfires">wildfires</a> throughout Southern California.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The current <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">Office of Management and Budget</a> (OMB) metropolitan designation for the <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County Area</a> is <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana%E2%80%93Anaheim%E2%80%93Irvine,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Ana\xe2\x80\x93Anaheim\xe2\x80\x93Irvine, California">Santa Ana\xe2\x80\x93Anaheim\xe2\x80\x93Irvine, California</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" people</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Santa_Ana,_California" title="Timeline of Santa Ana, California">Timeline of Santa Ana, California</a></div>\n<p>Members of the <a href="/wiki/Tongva_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tongva people">Tongva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juane%C3%B1o" title="Juane\xc3\xb1o">Juane\xc3\xb1o</a>/<a href="/wiki/Luise%C3%B1o_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Luise\xc3\xb1o people">Luise\xc3\xb1o</a> are indigenous to the area. The Tongva called the Santa Ana area "Hotuuk."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the 1769 expedition of <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_de_Portol%C3%A0" title="Gaspar de Portol\xc3\xa0">Gaspar de Portol\xc3\xa1</a> out of <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, then capitol of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>, Friar <a href="/wiki/Junipero_Serra" class="mw-redirect" title="Junipero Serra">Jun\xc3\xadpero Serra</a> named the area <b>Vallejo de Santa Ana</b> (Valley of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">Saint Anne</a>, or Santa Ana Valley). On November&#160;1, 1776, <a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Juan_Capistrano" title="Mission San Juan Capistrano">Mission San Juan Capistrano</a> was established within this valley. This Santa Ana Valley comprised most of what is now called Orange County.\n</p><p>In 1810, year of the commencement of the war of <a href="/wiki/Mexican_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican independence">Mexican Independence (1810\xe2\x80\x931821)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jose_Antonio_Yorba" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Antonio Yorba">Jose Antonio Yorba</a>, a sergeant of the Spanish army, was granted land that he called <a href="/wiki/Rancho_Santiago_de_Santa_Ana" title="Rancho Santiago de Santa Ana">Rancho Santiago de Santa Ana</a>. Yorba\'s rancho included the lands where the cities of <a href="/wiki/Olive,_California" title="Olive, California">Olive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange,_California" title="Orange, California">Orange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorba_Linda,_California" title="Yorba Linda, California">Yorba Linda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park,_California" title="Villa Park, California">Villa Park</a>, Santa Ana, <a href="/wiki/Tustin,_California" title="Tustin, California">Tustin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa,_California" title="Costa Mesa, California">Costa Mesa</a> and unincorporated <a href="/wiki/El_Modena,_California" title="El Modena, California">El Modena</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Heights" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Ana Heights">Santa Ana Heights</a>, are today. This rancho was the only land grant in Orange County granted under <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">Spanish Rule</a>. Surrounding land grants in Orange County were granted after Mexican Independence by the new government.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaAna-1887.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/SantaAna-1887.jpg/220px-SantaAna-1887.jpg" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/SantaAna-1887.jpg/330px-SantaAna-1887.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/SantaAna-1887.jpg/440px-SantaAna-1887.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="413" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaAna-1887.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Santa Ana, 1887</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaAna-1891.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/SantaAna-1891.jpg/220px-SantaAna-1891.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/SantaAna-1891.jpg/330px-SantaAna-1891.jpg 1.5x, <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Fe_Depot,_Santa_Ana,_1911.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Atchison,_Topeka_and_Santa_Fe_Railway" title="Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railway">Santa Fe</a> Depot, 1911</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg/220px-Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg/330px-Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg/440px-Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4018" data-file-height="2688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Ana_City_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old Santa Ana City Hall, built 1935</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Mexican-American_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican-American war">Mexican-American war</a> ended in 1848, <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> became part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and American settlers arrived in this area.\n</p><p>Claimed in 1869 by <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentuckian</a> William H. Spurgeon on land obtained from the descendents of <a href="/wiki/Jose_Antonio_Yorba" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Antonio Yorba">Jose Antonio Yorba</a>, Santa Ana was incorporated as a city in 1886 with a population of 2000 and in 1889 became the seat of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a>.\n</p><p>In 1877, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Pacific_Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Pacific Railroad">Southern Pacific Railroad</a> built a branch line from <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles</a> to Santa Ana, which offered free right of way, land for a depot, and $10,000 in cash to the railroad in exchange for terminating the line in Santa Ana and not neighboring <a href="/wiki/Tustin,_California" title="Tustin, California">Tustin</a>.  In 1887, the <a href="/wiki/California_Central_Railway" title="California Central Railway">California Central Railway</a> (which became a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/Atchison,_Topeka_and_Santa_Fe_Railway" title="Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railway">Atchison, Topeka and Santa Fe Railway</a> the following year) broke the Southern Pacific\'s local monopoly on rail travel, offering service between Los Angeles and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego, California">San Diego</a> by way of Santa Ana as a major intermediate station.  By 1905 the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Interurban_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Los Angeles Interurban Railway (page does not exist)">Los Angeles Interurban Railway</a>, a predecessor to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Electric_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Electric Railway">Pacific Electric Railway</a>, extended from Los Angeles to Santa Ana, running along Fourth Street downtown.<sup id="cite_ref-trains_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trains-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>  Firestone Boulevard, the first direct automobile route between Los Angeles and Santa Ana, opened in 1935; it was enlarged into the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Freeway" title="Santa Ana Freeway">Santa Ana Freeway</a> in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Santa Ana was the home of the original <a href="/wiki/Glenn_L._Martin_Company" title="Glenn L. Martin Company">Glenn L. Martin aviation company</a>, founded in 1912 before merging with the <a href="/wiki/Wright_Company" title="Wright Company">Wright Company</a> in 1916. Later, <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Luther_Martin" class="mw-redirect" title="Glenn Luther Martin">Glenn Luther Martin</a> created a second company of the same name in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> which eventually merged with the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Corporation" title="Lockheed Corporation">Lockheed Corporation</a> to form the largest defense contractor in the world, <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-santaanahistory.com_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-santaanahistory.com-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Army_Air_Base" title="Santa Ana Army Air Base">Santa Ana Army Air Base</a> was built as a training center for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">United States Army Air Forces</a>. The base was responsible for continued population growth in Santa Ana and the rest of Orange County as many veterans moved to the area to raise families after the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1958, Fashion Square Mall was built, adjoining the existing Bullock\'s Department Store building that was built in 1954. It opened north of downtown and became a major retail center for the area. In 1987, the mall was completely renovated and became MainPlace Mall (now Westfield MainPlace).\n</p><p>Having been a Charter City since November 11, 1952, the citizens of Santa Ana amended the Charter November 1988 to provide for the direct election of the Mayor who until that point had been appointed from the council membership. The current mayor of Santa Ana is <a href="/wiki/Miguel_A._Pulido" title="Miguel A. Pulido">Miguel A. Pulido</a>, the first mayor of Latino descent in the city\'s history and the first Mayor directly elected by the voters.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the 1980s, Santa Ana has been characterized by an effort to revitalize the <a href="/wiki/Downtown_National_Register_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown National Register District">downtown area</a> which had declined in influence. The Santa Ana Artist\'s Village was created around <a href="/wiki/Cal_State_Fullerton" class="mw-redirect" title="Cal State Fullerton">Cal State Fullerton</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/CSUF_Grand_Central_Art_Center" title="CSUF Grand Central Art Center">Grand Central Art Center</a> to attract artists and young professionals to live-work lofts and new businesses. The process has continued into 2009 with the reopening of the historic <a href="/wiki/Yost_Theater" title="Yost Theater">Yost Theater</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Santa Ana is located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;params=33_44_27_N_117_52_53_W_region:US-CA_type:city"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">33\xc2\xb044\xe2\x80\xb227\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">117\xc2\xb052\xe2\x80\xb253\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">33.74083\xc2\xb0N 117.88139\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">33.74083; -117.88139</span></span></span></a></span> (33.740717, -117.881408).<sup id="cite_ref-GR1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, the city has a total area of 27.5 square miles (71&#160;km<sup>2</sup>). 27.3 square miles (71&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of it is land and 0.2 square miles (0.52&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of it (0.90%) is water. It is the 4th most densely populated place in the United States with a population of 300,000 or more with 12,471.5 people per sq.&#160;mile.\n</p><p>Santa Ana is nested on flat, low-lying plains with little land elevation change. Running through the west end of the city is the mostly <a href="/wiki/River_engineering#Channelization" title="River engineering">channelized</a> <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_River" title="Santa Ana River">Santa Ana River</a>, which is also largely seasonal due to the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Prado_Dam" title="Prado Dam">Prado Dam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seven_Oaks_Dam" title="Seven Oaks Dam">Seven Oaks Dam</a>. The river has caused several severe floods in the 20th century, and is a continued threat despite the existence of the dams.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Now fully developed, Santa Ana has several distinct districts. The core of the city is the downtown area, which contains both retail and housing, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Civic_Center" title="Santa Ana Civic Center">Santa Ana Civic Center</a> which is a dense campus of administrative buildings for both the city and the county of Orange. The civic center is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Federal_Building_and_Courthouse_(California)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronald Reagan Federal Building and Courthouse (California)">Ronald Reagan Federal Building and Courthouse</a>. Several historic homes dating from the late 1800s can be found as well, and their preservation is a key issue as development of the downtown area continues.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>North of downtown is the "Midtown" district along Main St., home to entertainment destinations such as the <a href="/wiki/Bowers_Museum" title="Bowers Museum">Bowers Museum</a>, MainPlace Mall, and the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Science_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery Science Center">Discovery Science Center</a>.\n</p><p>Near the intersection of the Santa Ana Freeway and the <a href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa_Freeway" class="mw-redirect" title="Costa Mesa Freeway">Costa Mesa Freeway</a> is the newly designated "Metro East" area, which the city council has envisioned as a secondary <a href="/wiki/Mixed-use_development" title="Mixed-use development">mixed-use development</a> district.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Currently the area is occupied by several office towers, but little retail or housing. Also on the east side of the city is the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Zoo" title="Santa Ana Zoo">Santa Ana Zoo</a>, notable for its collection of <a href="/wiki/Monkeys" class="mw-redirect" title="Monkeys">monkeys</a> and species from <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>.\n</p><p>The southeast end of the city is part of the <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_Metro" title="South Coast Metro">South Coast Metro</a> area, which is shared with the city of <a href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa" class="mw-redirect" title="Costa Mesa">Costa Mesa</a>. <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_Plaza" title="South Coast Plaza">South Coast Plaza</a>, a major shopping center, is the primary destination of this area, which also contains several high-rise office and apartment buildings. Yokohama Tire Corporation\'s United States headquarters are located at 1 MacArthur Place in the South Coast Metro area of Santa Ana, and <a href="/wiki/Banc_of_California" title="Banc of California">Banc of California</a>\'s headquarters will relocate from neighboring Irvine to 3 MacArthur Place, Santa Ana, in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Santa Ana experiences a <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">hot semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen</a>: BSh), with hot, dry summers and mild winters with moderate rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The summer months of June to September average a daytime high of 83&#160;\xc2\xb0F (28.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C) and a nighttime low of 63&#160;\xc2\xb0F (17.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C). The winter months of December to March average a daytimehigh of 70&#160;\xc2\xb0F (21.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C) and a nighttime low of 48&#160;\xc2\xb0F (8.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C). Rainfall averages about 13.6&#160;in (345&#160;mm) per year, most of which falls from November through April. There are an average of 36 days with measurable precipitation annually.\n</p><p>The record high temperature for Santa Ana was 112&#160;\xc2\xb0F (44&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on June 14, 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDC_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDC-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  The record low temperature was 22&#160;\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x926&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on December 31, 1918, and January 1, 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDC_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDC-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  There are an average of 25.6 days with highs of 90&#160;\xc2\xb0F (32&#160;\xc2\xb0C) or higher and an average of 0.2 days with lows of 32&#160;\xc2\xb0F (0&#160;\xc2\xb0C) or lower.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDC_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDC-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The wettest year in Santa Ana was 1941 with 32.36 inches (822&#160;mm) and the driest year was 1961 with 3.55 inches (9.0&#160;cm).<sup id="cite_ref-WRCC_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRCC-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The most rainfall in one month was 13.99 inches (35.5&#160;cm) in February 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-WRCC_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRCC-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  The most rainfall in 24 hours was 4.69 inches (119&#160;mm) on February 16, 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-WRCC_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRCC-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; color:#000000;">1.0\n</td>\n<td style="background: #F7F7FF; color:#000000;">0.6\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FAFAFF; color:#000000;">0.4\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FAFAFF; color:#000000;">3.4\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B8B8FF; color:#000000;">5.7\n</td>\n<td style="background: #D9D9FF; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">35.8\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: NOAA (normals 1981\xe2\x80\x932010, extremes 1916\xe2\x80\x93present)<sup id="cite_ref-NCDC_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDC-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span data-file-width="3009" data-file-height="3009" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Santa_Ana_(5560450988).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of racial distribution in Santa Ana, 2010 U.S. Census. Each dot is 25 people: <span style="color:#ff0000"><b>White</b></span>, <span style="color:#0000ff"><b>Black</b></span>, <span style="color:#00ff80"><b>Asian</b></span>, <span style="color:#ff8000"><b>Hispanic</b></span> or <b>Other</b> (yellow)</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the California State Department of Finance, Demographic Research Unit, the current population for 2015 is 335,264.\nAs of 2015, 52,582 residents are enrolled in Santa Ana Unified School District K-12 schools with 11,156 resident students attending Garden Grove schools within Santa Ana and Garden Grove city limits in Garden Grove Unified School District.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_and_Figures_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_and_Figures-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the Orange County Registrar of Voters, 93,915 residents are registered to vote.\n</p><p>According to the State of California, Employment Development Department, 161,100 residents are a part of the civilian labor force.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> reported that Santa Ana had a population of 324,528. The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 11,793.3 people per square mile (4,553.4/km\xc2\xb2). The racial makeup of Santa Ana was 148,838 (45.9%) <a href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a> (9.2% <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Hispanic White">Non-Hispanic White</a>), 4,856 (1.5%) <a href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 3,260 (1.0%) <a href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 34,138 (10.5%) <a href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 976 (0.3%) <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 120,789 (37.2%) from <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (United States Census)">other races</a>, and 11,671 (3.6%) from two or more races.  <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 253,928 persons (78.2%).\n</p><p>The census reported that 319,870 people (98.6% of the population) lived in households, 1,415 (0.4%) lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 3,243 (1.0%) were institutionalized.\n</p><p>There were 73,174 households, out of which 41,181 (56.3%) had children under the age of 18 living in them, 41,389 (56.6%) were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">opposite-sex married couples</a> living together, 11,808 (16.1%) had a female householder with no husband present, 6,451 (8.8%) had a male householder with no wife present.  There were 4,933 (6.7%) <a href="/wiki/POSSLQ" title="POSSLQ">unmarried opposite-sex partnerships</a>, and 556 (0.8%) <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_partnerships" class="mw-redirect" title="Same-sex partnerships">same-sex married couples or partnerships</a>. 9,254 households (12.6%) were made up of individuals and 3,378 (4.6%) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 4.37.  There were 59,648 <a href="/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Family (U.S. Census)">families</a> (81.5% of all households); the average family size was 4.54.\n</p><p>The age distribution of the population was as follows: 99,678 people (30.7%) under the age of 18, 39,165 people (12.1%) aged 18 to 24, 102,399 people (31.6%) aged 25 to 44, 61,375 people (18.9%) aged 45 to 64, and 21,911 people (6.8%) who were 65 years of age or older.  The median age was 29.1 years. For every 100 females, there were 104.4 males.  For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 104.6 males.\n</p><p>There were 76,896 housing units at an average density of 2,794.4 per square mile (1,078.9/km\xc2\xb2), of which 34,756 (47.5%) were owner-occupied, and 38,418 (52.5%) were occupied by renters. The homeowner vacancy rate was 1.9%; the rental vacancy rate was 4.9%.  154,045 people (47.5% of the population) lived in owner-occupied housing units and 165,825 people (51.1%) lived in rental housing units.\n</p><p>During 2009\xe2\x80\x932013, Santa Ana had a median household income of $53,335, with 21.5% of the population living below the federal poverty line.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000">2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a><sup id="cite_ref-GR2_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> of 2000, there are 337,977 people, 73,002 households, and 59,788 families residing in the city.  The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> is 4,808.2/km\xc2\xb2 (12,451.9/mi\xc2\xb2).  There are 74,588 housing units at an average density of 1,061.1/km\xc2\xb2 (2,748.0/mi\xc2\xb2).  The racial makeup of the city is 42.73% <a href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 1.70% <a href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 1.19% <a href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 8.81% <a href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0.34% <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 40.64% from <a href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (U.S. Census)">other races</a>, and 4.58% from two or more races.  76.07% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race.\n</p><p>There are 73,002 households out of which 53.2% have children under the age of 18 living with them, 60.6% are <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 13.5% have a female householder with no husband present, and 18.1% are non-families. 12.7% of all households are made up of individuals and 4.6% have someone living alone who is 65 years of age or older.  The average household size is 4.55 and the average family size is 4.72.\n</p><p>In the city, the population is spread out with 34.2% under the age of 18, 12.8% from 18 to 24, 34.1% from 25 to 44, 13.5% from 45 to 64, and 5.5% who are 65 years of age or older.  The median age is 26 years.  For every 100 females, there are 107.7 males.  For every 100 females age 18 and over, there are 108.7 males.\n</p><p>The median income for a household from 2005-2009 was $54,521.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_and_Figures_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_and_Figures-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The median income for a household in the city is $43,412, and the median income for a family is $41,050. Males have a median income of $23,342 versus $21,637 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the city is $12,152.  19.8% of the population and 16.1% of families are below the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>.  Out of the total population, 24.1% of those under the age of 18 and 10.4% of those 65 and older are living below the poverty line.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(February 2009)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Santa Ana is the corporate headquarters of several companies including <a href="/wiki/Behr_Paint" class="mw-redirect" title="Behr Paint">Behr Paint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corinthian_Colleges" title="Corinthian Colleges">Corinthian Colleges</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_American_Corporation" title="First American Corporation">First American Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenwood_%26_Hall" title="Greenwood &amp; Hall">Greenwood &amp; Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingram_Micro" title="Ingram Micro">Ingram Micro</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Orange_County_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="The Orange County Register">The Orange County Register</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/SchoolsFirst_Federal_Credit_Union" title="SchoolsFirst Federal Credit Union">SchoolsFirst Federal Credit Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/STEC,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="STEC, Inc.">STEC</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=TTM_Technologies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="TTM Technologies (page does not exist)">TTM Technologies</a>, beverage company <a href="/wiki/Kern%27s_(beverage_company)" title="Kern&#39;s (beverage company)">Kern\'s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wahoo%27s_Fish_Taco" title="Wahoo&#39;s Fish Taco">Wahoo\'s Fish Taco</a>. It also houses major regional headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a> corporation, <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Software" title="Ultimate Software">Ultimate Software</a>, and <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a>. Nonprofits based in Santa Ana include <a href="/wiki/Open_Doors" title="Open Doors">Open Doors</a>.\n</p><p>One of Santa Ana\'s most notable businesses is the <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker" title="Rickenbacker">Rickenbacker</a> musical instrument company, whose <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">electric guitars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bass_guitar" title="Bass guitar">bass guitars</a> earned fame in the hands of many <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> legends.\n</p><p>Then <a href="/wiki/Glenn_L._Martin_Company" title="Glenn L. Martin Company">Glenn L. Martin Company</a>, a precursor to <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>, was founded in Santa Ana in 1912 before merging with the <a href="/wiki/Wright_Company" title="Wright Company">Wright Company</a> in 1916.\n</p><p>In recent years, the nearby city of <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine</a> has outpaced Santa Ana in commercial growth, with the Irvine Business District located near John Wayne Airport. To compete with this, Santa Ana has approved commercial projects in the <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_Metro" title="South Coast Metro">South Coast Metro</a> area, as well as the "Metro East" development, located at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Santa Ana Freeway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_55" title="California State Route 55">Costa Mesa Freeway</a>.\n</p><p>The Historic South Main Business District contains many older retail shops and other small businesses. It extends from downtown Santa Ana southwards on Main Street to the South Coast Metro area.\n</p><p>Santa Ana is part of a metropolitan area which includes Los Angeles and Long Beach. When it comes to <a href="/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product" title="Gross metropolitan product">gross metropolitan product</a> of U.S. metro areas, Los Angeles-Long Beach-Santa Ana, CA is ranked number two in 2013 with a GMP of $792.2 billion. When <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) and <a href="/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product" title="Gross metropolitan product">gross metropolitan product</a> (GMP) for country or metro area were compared, Los Angeles-Long Beach-Santa Ana, CA ranked number 20 for their 2013 numbers. The ranking for Santa Ana was higher than both Saudi Arabia and Switzerland, which ranked 21 and 22 respectively. The estimated annual growth rate of United States metro area economies from 2013-2020 is 2.9 percent with $686.5 billion in 2013 and an estimated $838.2 billion in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-usmayors.org_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usmayors.org-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to real gross metropolitan product and employment growth rates from 2013 to 2015, the Los Angeles-Long Beach-Santa Ana, CA metropolitan area ranked number two according to its 2013 GMP. Its percent change in employment was 1.7 in 2013, 1.1 in 2014, and 1.5 in 2015 and its percent change in real GMP 2.7 in 2013, 1.8 in 2014, and 2.6 in 2015. Real gross state and metropolitan output in terms of annual growth percentages in the metropolitan area of Los Angeles-Long Beach-Santa Ana, CA was 2.3 in 2014 and 3.3 in 2015.\nIn terms of end of the year value, the metro area unemployment rates in Los Angeles-Long Beach-Santa Ana, CA were 9.6 percent in 2012, 8.5 percent in 2013, 7.6 percent in 2014, and 7.0 percent in 2015, and will be approximately 6.7 percent in 2016. The unemployment growth rate from 2012 to 2016 is negative 2.9 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-usmayors.org_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usmayors.org-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was a recession in the last 2000s (decade) and the expected year for return to peak employment for the Los Angeles-Long Beach-Santa Ana, CA area is 2015. The pre-recession peak year was 2007. Due to the recession, 519.3 thousands of jobs were lost, this was a decline percent was 9.<sup id="cite_ref-usmayors.org_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usmayors.org-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> According to the Employment Development Department, the current unemployment rate for 2015 is 5 percent.\n</p><p>When it comes to building activity, the total valuation of all construction comes up to be $155,402,851.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Top_employers">Top employers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Center, TTM Technologies, Integrated Healthcare Holdings Inc, <a href="/wiki/Allied_Universal" title="Allied Universal">Allied Universal</a>, MSC Software Corp, and Sterns Learning Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_and_Figures_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_and_Figures-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Zawiya_Perpective.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Inside_Zawiya_Perpective.jpg/220px-Inside_Zawiya_Perpective.jpg" width="220" height="58" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Zawiya_Perpective.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inside Zawiya Perspective in Santa Ana, 2012</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation_and_attractions">Recreation and attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Recreation and attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Santa Ana has a number of parks.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  Disneyland and Knott\'s Berry Farm amusement parks are located northwest of Santa Ana, several kilometers away.  Beaches are located around 20 minutes to the south, accessible by the 55 freeway.  Huntington Beach and Newport Beach as well as other coastal communities offer shopping, dining, boating, swimming and surfing.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sites_of_interest">Sites of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sites of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">\n<ul><li>The Chiarini Fountain- Designed and Carved by Chiarini Marble &amp; Stone. Dontated by the Chiarini Family. In Honor of George C. Chiarini and to recognize those artists that have helped make Downtown Santa Ana a creative center in Orange County.</li>\n<li>Artist Village and Civic Center (See <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Santa_Ana_Historic_Districts" title="Downtown Santa Ana Historic Districts">Downtown Santa Ana Historic Districts</a>).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bowers_Museum" title="Bowers Museum">Bowers Museum</a> - Art and History museum started in the 1930s with a large collection of fine art and artifacts from around the world and several traveling exhibits each year.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/CSUF_Grand_Central_Art_Center" title="CSUF Grand Central Art Center">CSUF Grand Central Art Center</a> - At the heart of the Artist Village in Santa Ana.</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delhi_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Delhi Park (page does not exist)">Delhi Park</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Salvador_Park_(Artesia_Pilar_Neighborhood)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="El Salvador Park (Artesia Pilar Neighborhood) (page does not exist)">El Salvador Park (Artesia Pilar Neighborhood)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Discovery_Science_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery Science Center">Discovery Science Center</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Downtown_National_Register_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown National Register District">Downtown National Register District</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Downtown_Santa_Ana_Historic_Districts" title="Downtown Santa Ana Historic Districts">Downtown Santa Ana Historic Districts</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_Centro_Cultural_de_M%C3%A9xico" class="mw-redirect" title="El Centro Cultural de M\xc3\xa9xico">El Centro Cultural de M\xc3\xa9xico</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Main_Place_Mall" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Place Mall">Main Place Mall</a> opened in 1987.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Orange_County_Courthouse_(California)" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Orange County Courthouse (California)">Old Orange County Courthouse</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Civic_Center" title="Santa Ana Civic Center">Santa Ana Civic Center</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_College" title="Santa Ana College">Santa Ana College</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Rancho_Santiago_Community_College_District" title="Rancho Santiago Community College District">Rancho Santiago Community College District</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Zoo" title="Santa Ana Zoo">Santa Ana Zoo</a>, built in 1960.</li>\n<li>Greenville, a former rural part of Santa Ana, has buildings over a century old, but industrial complexes have replaced the agricultural fields once surrounding the town.</li></ul>\n<p>Santa Ana has several wall paintings and <a href="/wiki/Murals" class="mw-redirect" title="Murals">murals</a> depicting local history, community events and cultural diversity in Orange County.\n</p>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_locations">Notable locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 18em; -webkit-column-width: 18em; column-width: 18em;">\n<ul><li>The Chiarini Electric Sub-Station No. 14</a></li>\n<li>Southern (D), Builders Exchange Building</li>\n<li>Ronald W Reagan Federal Courthouse</li>\n<li>Newhope Branch Santa Ana Public Library</li>\n<li>Dr. Willella Regional Transportation Center</li>\n<li>McFadden Branch Santa Ana Public Learning Center</li>\n<li>Santora Building</li>\n<li>Heritage Museum of Orange County (Kellogg House)</li>\n<li><a Building</li>\n<li>Dexter\'s Chomp House</li>\n<li>Zawiya Perspective</li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg/220px-SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg/330px-SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg/440px-SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaAnaCityStadium1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>City Stadium, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Santa Ana has highly competitive high school and collegiate sports teams playing at <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Stadium" title="Santa Ana Stadium">Santa Ana Stadium</a> and the recently opened Santa Ana Unified School District Sports Complex Stadium. <a href="/wiki/Mater_Dei_High_School_(Santa_Ana,_California)" title="Mater Dei High School (Santa Ana, California)">Mater Dei High School</a> has one of the most successful and reputable American football programs in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_College" title="Santa Ana College">The Dons of Santa Ana College</a> are one of the most successful soccer teams in the state of California, and is a frequent top finisher, statewide.<sup id="cite_ref-sacdons.com_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sacdons.com-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, the Dons clinched their fifteenth consecutive <a href="/w/index.php?title=Orange_Empire_Conference_title&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Orange Empire Conference title (page does not exist)">Orange Empire Conference title</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sacdons.com_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sacdons.com-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The college is also known for its historically successful baseball teams,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and for producing former Texas Rangers and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/C._J._Wilson" title="C. J. Wilson">C. J. Wilson</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Santa Ana utilizes a <a href="/wiki/Council-Manager_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Council-Manager government">mayor-council</a> form of government.  The council consists of six members who are elected by the populace of the city.  Each member serves for four years and can serve a total of three terms. A <a href="/wiki/Pro_tempore#Mayor_pro_tem" title="Pro tempore">mayor pro tem</a> is elected by the council members from within the council.<sup id="cite_ref-gov_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mayor <a href="/wiki/Miguel_A._Pulido" title="Miguel A. Pulido">Miguel Pulido</a> is currently under investigation by the city attorney for a property swap involving a city contractor, in which the mayor ended up profiting $200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>  The mayor voted for a $1.4-million city contract with an auto parts firm, NAPA Orange County, just over a year after he bought a home from the firm\'s owner for $230,000 less than fair market value.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Santa Ana is one of a few cities in Orange County where <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> registration outnumbers that of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 Presidential Election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> in the city by a margin of 20,357 votes, 65% to 32%.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> This was despite Obama losing to fellow Democrat <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> in the city during the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)_presidential_primaries,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Party (United States) presidential primaries, 2008">Democratic Primary</a>.  Despite the city\'s high percentage of Democrats, however, the city tends to vote conservatively on social issues, much like the rest of northern Orange County.  It voted Yes on <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8" class="mw-redirect" title="California Proposition 8">Proposition 8</a>\xe2\x80\x94California\'s amendment defining marriage in the state as a legal union between a man and a woman\xe2\x80\x94by 61.9%, above the county\'s average of 57.7%.  On <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_4_(2008)" title="California Proposition 4 (2008)">Proposition 4</a>, which would have amended the <a href="/wiki/California_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="California Constitution">California Constitution</a> to require minors to notify their parents before having an abortion, Santa Ana voted in favor of the measure by 62.0%, much higher than the county as a whole, which voted in favor of the measure by only 54.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Legislature" title="California State Legislature">California State Legislature</a>, Santa Ana is in <a href="/wiki/California%27s_34th_State_Senate_district" title="California&#39;s 34th State Senate district">the  34th Senate District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">Republican</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Janet_Nguyen" title="Janet Nguyen">Janet Nguyen</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/California%27s_69th_State_Assembly_district" title="California&#39;s 69th State Assembly district">the  69th Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Tom_Daly_(American_politician)" title="Tom Daly (American politician)">Tom Daly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>, Santa Ana is split between <a href="/wiki/California%27s_46th_congressional_district" title="California&#39;s 46th congressional district">California\'s  46th congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Lou_Correa" title="Lou Correa">Lou Correa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California%27s_48th_congressional_district" title="California&#39;s 48th congressional district">California\'s  48th congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Dana_Rohrabacher" title="Dana Rohrabacher">Dana Rohrabacher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_missions_of_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic missions of Mexico">Consulate-General of Mexico in Santa Ana</a> is located on 828&#160;North Broadway Street.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_missions_of_El_Salvador" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic missions of El Salvador">Consulate-General of El Salvador in Santa Ana</a> is located in Suite&#160;103 at 840&#160;North Grand Avenue.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School,_Santa_Ana,_Nov._1932.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School%2C_Santa_Ana%2C_Nov._1932.jpg/220px-Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School%2C_Santa_Ana%2C_Nov._1932.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School%2C_Santa_Ana%2C_Nov._1932.jpg/330px-Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School%2C_Santa_Ana%2C_Nov._1932.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School%2C_Santa_Ana%2C_Nov._1932.jpg/440px-Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School%2C_Santa_Ana%2C_Nov._1932.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5665" data-file-height="3493" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Julia_Lathrop_Junior_High_School,_Santa_Ana,_Nov._1932.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Julia_Lathrop" title="Julia Lathrop">Julia Lathrop</a> Junior High School, Santa Ana, 1932</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Unified_School_District" title="Santa Ana Unified School District">Santa Ana Unified School District</a> includes thirty-seven K\xe2\x80\x935 elementary schools, nine 6\xe2\x80\x938 intermediate schools, eight 9\xe2\x80\x9312 high schools, five special schools, and one charter school. Some elementary schools are: John Adams Elementary School, Manuel Esqueda Elementary School, Diamond Elementary School.\nThe school district provides an online accountability report card.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Garden_Grove_Unified_School_District" title="Garden Grove Unified School District">Garden Grove Unified School District</a> also includes some schools within Santa Ana.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Unified_School_District" title="Santa Ana Unified School District">Santa Ana Unified School District</a>\'s public high schools include <a href="/wiki/Valley_High_School_(Santa_Ana)" class="mw-redirect" title="Valley High School (Santa Ana)">Valley High School (Santa Ana)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_College_High_School_(Santa_Ana)" title="Middle College High School (Santa Ana)">Middle College High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_High_School" title="Santa Ana High School">Santa Ana High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saddleback_High_School" title="Saddleback High School">Saddleback High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Century_High_School_(Santa_Ana,_California)" title="Century High School (Santa Ana, California)">Century High School</a>, newly opened <a href="/wiki/Segerstrom_Fundamental_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Segerstrom Fundamental High School">Segerstrom Fundamental High School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Godinez_Fundamental_High_School" title="Godinez Fundamental High School">Godinez Fundamental High School</a>, and other public schools in the area, along with the <a href="/wiki/Orange_County_High_School_of_the_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange County High School of the Arts">Orange County High School of the Arts</a> in the midtown district.\n</p><p>The Roman Catholic Diocese operates <a href="/wiki/Mater_Dei_High_School,_Santa_Ana" class="mw-redirect" title="Mater Dei High School, Santa Ana">Mater Dei High School</a>.  The Diocese also operates several K\xe2\x80\x938 schools in Santa Ana, including School of Our Lady, Saint Anne, Saint Barbara, and Saint Joseph. (Immaculate Heart Of Mary And Our Lady Of the Pillar schools were closed in 2005 and merged into the School of Our Lady, which is located at Immaculate Heart of Mary Parish.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In September 2005 the Orange County Campus of <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Los_Angeles" title="International School of Los Angeles">International School of Los Angeles</a> (LILA) moved to Santa Ana.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In July 2015 it moved back to <a href="/wiki/Orange,_California" title="Orange, California">Orange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is home to <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_College" title="Santa Ana College">Santa Ana College</a>, a two-year public <a href="/wiki/Community_colleges_in_the_United_States" title="Community colleges in the United States">community college</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/California_Coast_University" title="California Coast University">California Coast University</a>, and the Orange County branch of the <a href="/wiki/Art_Institute_of_California_-_Orange_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Art Institute of California - Orange County">Art Institute of California</a>. <a href="/wiki/Taft_Law_School" title="Taft Law School">Taft Law School</a> a correspondence law school is also based in Santa Ana. <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Law_School" title="Trinity Law School">Trinity Law School</a> is a Christian, CBE-accredited law school that is the only California campus of the <a href="/wiki/Trinity_International_University" title="Trinity International University">Trinity International University</a> system of schools. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Detective_Training_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Detective Training Institute (page does not exist)">Detective Training Institute</a> is a correspondence/distance learning institution that offers private investigator diplomas and is approved to operate by the Bureau for Private Postsecondary Education. <a href="/wiki/Career_Networks_Institute_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Career Networks Institute College">Career Networks Institute College</a> is a post secondary occupational learning center for allied health is also based in the city.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A few freeways run through Santa Ana, connecting the city to other areas in Orange County, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">Greater Los Angeles Area</a>, and beyond. The <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Freeway" title="Santa Ana Freeway">Santa Ana Freeway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Interstate 5</a>) heads north to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and south towards Southern Orange County and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>. The <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_22" title="California State Route 22">Garden Grove Freeway (State Route 22)</a> runs along near Santa Ana\'s northern border, connecting <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California" title="Long Beach, California">Long Beach</a> to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Orange,_California" title="Orange, California">City of Orange</a> to the east. The <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_55" title="California State Route 55">Costa Mesa Freeway (State Route 55)</a> travels south to <a href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa,_California" title="Costa Mesa, California">Costa Mesa</a>; and then north to the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_91" title="California State Route 91">Riverside Freeway (State Route 91)</a>, providing a connection to <a href="/wiki/Riverside,_California" title="Riverside, California">Riverside</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, the national passenger rail system, provides service to Santa Ana several times on weekdays with less frequent service on weekends. It operates its <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Surfliner" title="Pacific Surfliner">Pacific Surfliner</a> between <a href="/wiki/San_Diego,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego, California">San Diego</a> to the south and either <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles</a> or <a href="/wiki/Paso_Robles,_California" title="Paso Robles, California">Paso Robles</a> to the north (see <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_(Amtrak_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Ana (Amtrak station)">Santa Ana Regional Transportation Center</a>). Greyhound USA is the largest bus transportation service in Santa Ana. Greyhound serves the continental United States and Canada. The bus lines Crucero, Intercalifornias, and others serve all points into Mexico.\n</p><p>Santa Ana is also served by <a href="/wiki/Metrolink_(Southern_California)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metrolink (Southern California)">Metrolink\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Metrolink_Orange_County_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Metrolink Orange County Line">Orange County Line</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oceanside,_California" title="Oceanside, California">Oceanside</a> to <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Los_Angeles)" title="Union Station (Los Angeles)">Union Station</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Metrolink_Inland_Empire-Orange_County_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Metrolink Inland Empire-Orange County Line">Inland Empire-Orange County Line</a> (<a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino,_California" title="San Bernardino, California">San Bernardino</a> to <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Capistrano,_California" title="San Juan Capistrano, California">San Juan Capistrano</a>).\n</p><p>Santa Ana is in the preliminary stages of implementing a street car system that will connect the Santa Ana Train station to Downtown Santa Ana.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Public transit bus service is available via the <a href="/wiki/Orange_County_Transportation_Authority" title="Orange County Transportation Authority">Orange County Transportation Authority</a> (OCTA).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Wayne_Airport" title="John Wayne Airport">John Wayne Airport</a> is located at 18601 Airport Way Santa Ana, CA 92707. The <a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a> code for the airport is SNA.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Electricity for the city is provided by <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Edison" title="Southern California Edison">Southern California Edison</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Gas_Company" title="Southern California Gas Company">Southern California Gas Company</a> provides natural gas service.  Phone and cable television is provided by <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="AT&amp;T Inc.">AT&amp;T</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_service">Emergency service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Emergency service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Law enforcement is provided by the Santa Ana Police Department from three stations throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>  The department includes five canine units,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> an 11 officer <a href="/wiki/Mounted_police" title="Mounted police">equestrian unit</a> and a 37-member <a href="/wiki/SWAT" title="SWAT">SWAT</a> team.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>  The city shares a helicopter with the cities of <a href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa,_California" title="Costa Mesa, California">Costa Mesa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Beach, California">Newport Beach</a> via the Airborne Law Enforcement (ABLE) program.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2012, the city disbanded its municipal fire department which had provided fire protection for 128 years<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and contracted with the <a href="/wiki/Orange_County_Fire_Authority" title="Orange County Fire Authority">Orange County Fire Authority</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Ana,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Santa_Ana,_California" title="List of people from Santa Ana, California">List of people from Santa Ana, California</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
